<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2014 Southeast Europe floods</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Deaths</th>
<td style="text-align: left;">
<p><b>At least 86</b><br/>
<small>57 in Serbia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><br/>
24 in Bosnia and Herzegovina<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><br/>
2 in Croatia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ajb001_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-ajb001-5">[5]</a></sup><br/>
2 in Romania<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alexandra_Ciliac_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alexandra_Ciliac-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><br/>
1 in Slovakia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agerpres_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-agerpres-8">[8]</a></sup><br/></small></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Property damage</th>
<td style="text-align: left;">More than one billion <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euros</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Between 13 and 18 May 2014 a low-pressure <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclone</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> designated <i>Tamara</i> and <i>Yvette</i> affected a large area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, causing floods and landslides. <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> suffered the greatest damage, as the rain was the heaviest in 120 years of recorded weather measurements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> By 20 May, at least 62 people had died as a result of the flooding, and hundreds of thousands had been forced from their homes. Towns of <a href="/wiki/Obrenovac" title="Obrenovac">Obrenovac</a> in Serbia and <a href="/wiki/Doboj" title="Doboj">Doboj</a> in Bosnia and Herzegovina account for most victims, after being inundated by several meters high waters from nearby rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Floodwaters caused over 2,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landslides" title="Landslides">landslides</a> across the Balkan region, spreading damage across many towns and villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flee_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-flee-14">[14]</a></sup> The rains activated torrents and mudslides, and subsequently several rivers in watersheds of <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Morava" title="Great Morava">Morava</a> rose and flooded surrounding valleys. Official counts indicate that over 1.6 million people were affected in Serbia and Bosnia, after a week of flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Assessments of the damage range up to 3.5 billions € for Serbia, Bosnia and Herzegovina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Damage in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, jointly estimated by EU, World Bank group and UN officials, stands at 1,55 billion euros.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Officials in Bosnia stated that the damage could exceed that of the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The events initiated a large international aid campaign, with numerous countries, organizations and individuals donating humanitarian, material and monetary support for the affected areas.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NWS-NOAA_Europe_Total_Percipitation_MAY_11-17,_2014.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2250" data-file-width="2400" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NWS-NOAA_Europe_Total_Percipitation_MAY_11-17%2C_2014.png/220px-NWS-NOAA_Europe_Total_Percipitation_MAY_11-17%2C_2014.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NWS-NOAA_Europe_Total_Percipitation_MAY_11-17%2C_2014.png/330px-NWS-NOAA_Europe_Total_Percipitation_MAY_11-17%2C_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NWS-NOAA_Europe_Total_Percipitation_MAY_11-17%2C_2014.png/440px-NWS-NOAA_Europe_Total_Percipitation_MAY_11-17%2C_2014.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NWS-NOAA_Europe_Total_Percipitation_MAY_11-17,_2014.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Total precipitation between 11 and 17 May</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 13 May, a <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low-pressure area</a> formed over the Adriatic Sea, as polar air from Central Europe penetrated into the Mediterranean basin. The cold polar air mass met with humid subtropical air, leading to very low pressure. On 14 May, the low moved over the Balkans, becoming stationary. As a result, extremely heavy rain fell within the region; Serbia (in the area around Belgrade) and Bosnia were most affected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Serbian and Bosnian meteorologists named the formed <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclone</a> "Tamara".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tamara_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-tamara-21">[21]</a></sup> On 15 May, the daily amounts of rainfall broke historical records in Belgrade (107.9 mm), Valjevo (108.2 mm) and Loznica (110 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> By 15 May, the monthly rainfall in Belgrade had broken the historical record (175 l from 1897), reaching 205 l.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> By Saturday, May 17, the rain had subsided, and the weather gradually became warmer and sunnier, somewhat easing relief and rescue efforts. On 18 May, the cyclone moved further northwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tamara_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-tamara-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BosniaSerbiaflood.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/BosniaSerbiaflood.jpg/250px-BosniaSerbiaflood.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/BosniaSerbiaflood.jpg/375px-BosniaSerbiaflood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/BosniaSerbiaflood.jpg/500px-BosniaSerbiaflood.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BosniaSerbiaflood.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Severe flooding in the Balkans seen by the Moderate Resolution Imaging Spectroradiometer (MODIS) on <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s Aqua satellite, 19 May 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main flooding region was the watershed of the <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> river, which forms a border between Bosnia and Croatia, flows into Serbia, and drains into the Danube in Belgrade. On Wednesday, 14 May, heavy rainfall caused <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torrent_(stream)" title="Torrent (stream)">torrential</a> floods across mountainous regions, which destroyed bridges and infrastructure, and caused numerous <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a>. The deadliest impact occurred on Thursday, 15 May, when water levels in several right-bank tributaries of the Sava suddenly and uncontrollably rose at an unprecedented rate, flooding towns in their valleys. The <a href="/wiki/Bosna_(river)" title="Bosna (river)">Bosna</a> river in central Bosnia completely flooded the cities of <a href="/wiki/Doboj" title="Doboj">Doboj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maglaj" title="Maglaj">Maglaj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zavidovi%C4%87i" title="Zavidovići">Zavidovići</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0amac,_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Šamac, Bosnia and Herzegovina">Šamac</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Kolubara" title="Kolubara">Kolubara</a>, near Belgrade, did the same to <a href="/wiki/Obrenovac" title="Obrenovac">Obrenovac</a>; those cities had the major share of victims. Subsequently, the Sava itself rose to record-high levels, threatening the cities of <a href="/wiki/Slavonski_Brod" title="Slavonski Brod">Slavonski Brod</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0abac" title="Šabac">Šabac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Mitrovica" title="Sremska Mitrovica">Sremska Mitrovica</a> and numerous villages, but the damage was relatively contained as the population, helped by army and volunteers, strengthened <a href="/wiki/Flood_control" title="Flood control">flood defenses</a>. Nonetheless, <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">embankments</a> gave way in several places.</p>
<p>Heavy rainfall was also experienced in the region on 3 and 4 May, affecting Romania, Italy and Bosnia. The event produced limited damage but left a number of flooding incidents and high rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> A state of emergency was declared in parts of Bosnia by local government.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Affected_regions">Affected regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Affected regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Balkan_floods_May_2014.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Balkan_floods_May_2014.svg/300px-Balkan_floods_May_2014.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Balkan_floods_May_2014.svg/450px-Balkan_floods_May_2014.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Balkan_floods_May_2014.svg/600px-Balkan_floods_May_2014.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Balkan_floods_May_2014.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Affected areas of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>:
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff6363; color:black; font-size:60%; text-align:center;"> </span> Most affected areas</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffb7b7; color:black; font-size:60%; text-align:center;"> </span> Also affected</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Serbia was the most severely affected, with several major cities in its central region completely flooded, and landslides in mountainous regions. Bosnia, in particular its Republika Srpska entity, was also inundated to a crippling extent. Eastern Croatia and southern Romania also experienced flooding and human victims, while Austria, Bulgaria, Hungary, Italy, Poland and Slovakia were affected by the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poplava_obrenovac_2014_popovi%C4%87_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1840" data-file-width="3264" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Poplava_obrenovac_2014_popovi%C4%87_3.jpg/220px-Poplava_obrenovac_2014_popovi%C4%87_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Poplava_obrenovac_2014_popovi%C4%87_3.jpg/330px-Poplava_obrenovac_2014_popovi%C4%87_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Poplava_obrenovac_2014_popovi%C4%87_3.jpg/440px-Poplava_obrenovac_2014_popovi%C4%87_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Poplava_obrenovac_2014_popovi%C4%87_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Obrenovac" title="Obrenovac">Obrenovac</a> suffered the largest number of casualties and destruction during the flooding</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of <a href="/wiki/Obrenovac" title="Obrenovac">Obrenovac</a> was hit hardest by the floods, with an estimated 90% of the town flooded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-26">[26]</a></sup> During the night between 15 and 16 May, nearby <a href="/wiki/Kolubara" title="Kolubara">Kolubara</a> river, collecting waters from southerly mountains, suddenly rose several meters above its banks and flooded the city, catching the residents by surprise. The entire city was evacuated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b92_may21_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-b92_may21-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-28">[28]</a></sup> During 18 May, the water level dropped, which enabled the evacuation of the citizens of Obrenovac to be carried out by trucks instead of boats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> As of 20 May the total number of evacuated persons exceeded 30,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Krupanj_2014_-_by_Zoran_Dobrin_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Krupanj_2014_-_by_Zoran_Dobrin_1.jpg/220px-Krupanj_2014_-_by_Zoran_Dobrin_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Krupanj_2014_-_by_Zoran_Dobrin_1.jpg/330px-Krupanj_2014_-_by_Zoran_Dobrin_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Krupanj_2014_-_by_Zoran_Dobrin_1.jpg/440px-Krupanj_2014_-_by_Zoran_Dobrin_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Krupanj_2014_-_by_Zoran_Dobrin_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Destruction of <a href="/wiki/Krupanj" title="Krupanj">Krupanj</a> by a flood</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Krupanj" title="Krupanj">Krupanj</a> in western Serbia (located in a valley of several small rivers) torrents, mudslides and landslides devastated the infrastructure and destroyed dozens of houses. Because of road damages, the town was completely inaccessible for three days, and the road to Loznica was blocked until 18 May. Electric power was cut for almost the whole municipality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Around 500 houses were seriously damaged and at least 20 houses are completely uninhabitable <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Part of the village of <a href="/wiki/Rebelj" title="Rebelj">Rebelj</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valjevo" title="Valjevo">Valjevo</a> municipality was annihilated by landslides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Drina" title="Drina">Drina</a> river valley, on the border with Bosnia, heavy rain activated landslides, cutting off several villages and closing roads. At <a href="/wiki/Mali_Zvornik" title="Mali Zvornik">Mali Zvornik</a>, a giant hill threatened to slide into the river and cut its flow, endangering that town and <a href="/wiki/Zvornik" title="Zvornik">Zvornik</a> across the river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b92_may21_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-b92_may21-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Peak flood waters from <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> river hit <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0abac" title="Šabac">Šabac</a> on 18 May, but the embankments survived, strengthened by efforts of the army and several thousands volunteers. Flood waters on the river reached 6.3 metres (21 ft), the highest on record, endangering Šabac and <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Mitrovica" title="Sremska Mitrovica">Sremska Mitrovica</a> on the left bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-26">[26]</a></sup> In anticipation of the floods, a 7.3-metre (24 ft) temporary embankment was erected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Further east, along the valleys of <a href="/wiki/Great_Morava" title="Great Morava">Morava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mlava" title="Mlava">Mlava</a> rivers, city centers of <a href="/wiki/Para%C4%87in" title="Paraćin">Paraćin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrovac_na_Mlavi" title="Petrovac na Mlavi">Petrovac na Mlavi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Svilajnac" title="Svilajnac">Svilajnac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smederevska_Palanka" title="Smederevska Palanka">Smederevska Palanka</a> were flooded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the flooding period, an estimated 300,000 households were left without electric power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rfe_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-rfe-36">[36]</a></sup> Serbia's energy minister, Aleksandar Antić, has appealed to individuals to conserve power as best they can.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flee_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-flee-14">[14]</a></sup> The largest thermoelectric power plant in Serbia, <a href="/wiki/TPP_Nikola_Tesla" title="TPP Nikola Tesla">TPP Nikola Tesla</a>, which supplies close to 50% of electricity in Serbia, lies in the vicinity of Obrenovac, but was saved from danger. However, flood waters filled the largest coal field of <a href="/wiki/RB_Kolubara" title="RB Kolubara">RB Kolubara</a> with 210 million cubic meters of water, more than the volume of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vlasina_lake" title="Vlasina lake">Vlasina lake</a>, and its pumping out is expected to take months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rts_may21_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-rts_may21-37">[37]</a></sup> Further east, the thermoelectric power plant <a href="/wiki/Kostolac#Industry" title="Kostolac">TPP Kostolac</a>, which supplies 11% of electricity in Serbia, was threatened by floods from the <a href="/wiki/Mlava" title="Mlava">Mlava</a> river, but the water had not breached the innermost ring of defenses. During the floods, the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Gate_I_Hydroelectric_Power_Station" title="Iron Gate I Hydroelectric Power Station">hydro plants at Iron Gates</a> reduced their production and opened the gates in order to lower the level of the Danube.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rts_may21_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-rts_may21-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the floods, transport across the country, particularly central and western parts, was interrupted or broken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RVoR_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-RVoR-38">[38]</a></sup> 2,260 public, industrial and infrastructure facilities were flooded, and 3,500 roads were destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b92_may21_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-b92_may21-27">[27]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Bar_railway" title="Belgrade–Bar railway">Belgrade–Bar railway</a> was severed at several locations in western Serbia, and has been closed; basic reparations took about a month to complete, and afterwards the trains were forced to take a several-hours detour. Reconstruction of the section in the <a href="/wiki/Gradac_(river)" title="Gradac (river)">Gradac</a> river canyon was finished in March 2015, allowing the trains to return to the original route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Agricultural damage in affected areas was total, and the amount is yet to be determined. Thousands of cows, sheep, chicken and other domestic animals perished in the floods, and their corpses present a serious health risk for people who started returning and repairing their homes.</p>
<p>On 20 May, the Government of Serbia proclaimed 3 days of mourning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b92_may21_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-b92_may21-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Serbia" title="Prime Minister of Serbia">Serbian Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Vu%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Vučić">Aleksandar Vučić</a> described the flooding as "the worst natural catastrophe that has ever hit Serbia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RVoR_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-RVoR-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a July 2014 report by the Government of Serbia, the total amount of damage in the country was estimated at 1.53 billion Euro. Of those, 810 million was attributed to direct damage, and 662 million to losses. Two thirds of the damage was attributed to the production sector (500 million direct and 569 million indirect), of which 228 million in the agricultural sector. Total damage on the housing was 227.3 million, while the infrastructure damage (transportation, communications and water management) was assessed at 192 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Bosnia and Herzegovina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_floods_Kamerovica_flied.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/2014_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_floods_Kamerovica_flied.jpg/220px-2014_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_floods_Kamerovica_flied.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/2014_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_floods_Kamerovica_flied.jpg/330px-2014_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_floods_Kamerovica_flied.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/2014_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_floods_Kamerovica_flied.jpg/440px-2014_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_floods_Kamerovica_flied.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_floods_Kamerovica_flied.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flooding in <a href="/wiki/Zenica" title="Zenica">Zenica</a>, 15 May 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of northern Bosnia was flooded, with the Bosna river valley hit hardest. Other affected areas included <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Canton" title="Sarajevo Canton">Sarajevo Canton</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pobjeda_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-pobjeda-43">[43]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tuzla_Canton" title="Tuzla Canton">Tuzla</a>. Northern and northeastern Bosnia, including the region of <a href="/wiki/Semberija" title="Semberija">Semberija</a>, was also flooded. Rivers that flooded included the Bosna, <a href="/wiki/Vrbas_(river)" title="Vrbas (river)">Vrbas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drina" title="Drina">Drina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sana_(river)" title="Sana (river)">Sana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a>. A state of emergency was declared across the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Herzegovina" title="Herzegovina">Herzegovina</a> in the south and central regions were not hit by floods.</p>
<p>The town of <a href="/wiki/Maglaj" title="Maglaj">Maglaj</a> experienced the average rainfall of two months in under 48 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-26">[26]</a></sup> In the city of <a href="/wiki/Zavidovi%C4%87i" title="Zavidovići">Zavidovići</a>, a footbridge was filmed being swept down the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosna_river" title="Bosna river">Bosna river</a> and crashing into another bridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Miljacka" title="Miljacka">Miljacka</a> river swelled almost to the level of city bridges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pobjeda_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-pobjeda-43">[43]</a></sup> The entire hamlet of Parići in <a href="/wiki/Hrasno_Donje" title="Hrasno Donje">Hrasno Donje</a>, municipality of <a href="/wiki/Kalesija" title="Kalesija">Kalesija</a>, was swept away by landslides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 20 May, there were 24 confirmed deaths in Bosnia and Herzegovina: 17 in <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a> and 7 in the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Federation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnevnik.hr_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-dnevnik.hr-46">[46]</a></sup> At a press conference on 19 May, the Director of Police of Republika Srpska gave the names of 17 confirmed victims: 10 in Doboj, 2 in Šamac, 2 in <a href="/wiki/Modri%C4%8Da" title="Modriča">Modriča</a> and one each in <a href="/wiki/Bijeljina" title="Bijeljina">Bijeljina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlasenica" title="Vlasenica">Vlasenica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donji_%C5%BDabar" title="Donji Žabar">Donji Žabar</a>; an additional 7 persons are still listed as missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Governments of the two entities jointly declared 20 May a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mourning_day" title="Mourning day">day of mourning</a> across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnevnik.hr_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-dnevnik.hr-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was speculated that the floodwaters might have disturbed <a href="/wiki/Land_mine" title="Land mine">land mines</a> left over from the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a> (1992–95) which could cause further danger if moved outside the marked areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flee_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-flee-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The chief executive of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljeznice_Republike_Srpske" title="Željeznice Republike Srpske">Željeznice Republike Srpske</a>, the railway operator in <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a> (one of two railway operators in Bosnia) appealed for help in repairing the enormous damage to the railways in the country, stating that they were independently unable to repair the damage, appealing for help from the international community in supplying materials, mechanisation and financial assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Croatia">Croatia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Croatia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Floods_Croatia_2014..jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="568" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Floods_Croatia_2014..jpg/250px-Floods_Croatia_2014..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Floods_Croatia_2014..jpg/375px-Floods_Croatia_2014..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Floods_Croatia_2014..jpg/500px-Floods_Croatia_2014..jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Floods_Croatia_2014..jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Floods in <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>; red dots indicate ruptured embankents</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Floods_in_Croatia_Gunja_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="960" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Floods_in_Croatia_Gunja_2.jpg/250px-Floods_in_Croatia_Gunja_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Floods_in_Croatia_Gunja_2.jpg/375px-Floods_in_Croatia_Gunja_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Floods_in_Croatia_Gunja_2.jpg/500px-Floods_in_Croatia_Gunja_2.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Floods_in_Croatia_Gunja_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Severe flooding in the Croatian locality of Gunja</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Croatia was affected by the floods to a lesser extent than Serbia or Bosnia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The most critical area was in southern <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">Slavonia</a>. The embankment on the Sava River was breached near <a href="/wiki/Rajevo_Selo" title="Rajevo Selo">Rajevo Selo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ra%C4%8Dinovci" title="Račinovci">Račinovci</a>, and thus evacuation was ordered for <a href="/wiki/Gunja,_Croatia" title="Gunja, Croatia">Gunja</a>, Rajevo Selo and Račinovci. As of 19 May, around 15,000 people in easternmost parts of Croatia were evacuated from their homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indexhrevak_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-indexhrevak-50">[50]</a></sup> One of the most critical points was the embankment of the Sava river in <a href="/wiki/Slavonski_%C5%A0amac" title="Slavonski Šamac">Slavonski Šamac</a>, where the confluence of the Bosna and Sava is located. At that point the embankments were under severe pressure caused by the huge amount of water coming from Bosnia. Several officials stated that if this embankment were breached, the entire region of southern Slavonia, with a population of over 300 000, would be flooded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> There were also floods in <a href="/wiki/Banovina_(region)" title="Banovina (region)">Banovina</a> region, in the towns of <a href="/wiki/Hrvatska_Kostajnica" title="Hrvatska Kostajnica">Hrvatska Kostajnica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dvor,_Croatia" title="Dvor, Croatia">Dvor</a>, mostly caused by the river Una, whose level had not been as high since 1955.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DPRERADUS_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-DPRERADUS-52">[52]</a></sup> Video: <a class="external free" href="http://vimeo.com/96164094" rel="nofollow">http://vimeo.com/96164094</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This was the third major flood to hit <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> since late April 2014. Over 8,000 people were isolated and nearly 2,000 hectares of land were covered by water. 125 villages were affected by floods in one day. In total, 30 national and county roads were closed or partially destroyed by water and mud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The waters of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> rose so much that the authorities set orange code for flooding for eight days, on the sector <a href="/wiki/Iron_Gates" title="Iron Gates">Iron Gates</a>–<a href="/wiki/Zimnicea" title="Zimnicea">Zimnicea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Vrancea_County" title="Vrancea County">Vrancea County</a>, a 50-year-old man was carried away by the flood and found dead the next morning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alexandra_Ciliac_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Alexandra_Ciliac-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> was devastated by a <a href="/wiki/Storm" title="Storm">storm</a> accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">hail</a> and strong winds. Several streets were flooded, trees were uprooted, and a thick layer of ice covered important transport arteries, paralyzing the traffic in the capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovakia">Slovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Slovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Floods and strong winds from the cyclone also reached Slovakia, where an elderly man drowned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agerpres_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-agerpres-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_response">International response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: International response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Many countries and international organizations have offered to provide relief.</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="700" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/21px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/32px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/42px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png 2x" width="21"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> — Albania sent five search and rescue units to Bosnia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> — Austria sent a civil defense rescue team with high capacity pump to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanjug_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-tanjug-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> — The Government of Azerbaijan sent 40 tonnes of humanitarian aid to the affected population in Bosnia and Herzegovina. Additionally, humanitarian aid was sent to people in critical areas in Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The Government of Azerbaijan also stated that they would donate €400,000 to Serbia's flood relief fund.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="900" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Flag_of_Belarus.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belarus.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Flag_of_Belarus.svg/35px-Flag_of_Belarus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Flag_of_Belarus.svg/46px-Flag_of_Belarus.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> — President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lukashenko" title="Lukashenko">Lukashenko</a> ordered that help be sent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Belarus sent a first contingent to Serbia which amongst other material contained two helicopters with four teams of rescuers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-belarus_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-belarus-61">[61]</a></sup> The second contingent included four generators of 100 kilowatts, 20 other generators, 30 pumps for water, 20,000 cans of food, 5,000 blankets, 20 tents for 20 people each, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> — Belgium sent the <a href="/wiki/B-FAST" title="B-FAST">B-Fast team</a>, with a convoy of 10 trucks carrying a water treatment installation and pumps to provide drinkable water to the population in <a href="/wiki/Ora%C5%A1je" title="Orašje">Orašje</a>, Bosnia and Herzegovina. A second mission, with rescue boats for Serbia, will not depart, since the Serbian government has announced that plenty of boats are present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-belgium1_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-belgium1-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-belgium2_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-belgium2-64">[64]</a></sup><br/>
Bosnian expats in <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a> gathered 40 <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">metric tons</a> of relief goods, to be sent to Bosnia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deurne_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-deurne-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> — Bulgaria sent two fire engines with 10 motor pumps and more vehicles with 16 high-capacity water pumps and two boats to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanjug_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-tanjug-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> - The Government of Canada provided CAD800,000 in assistance in the aftermath of the catastrophic flooding. Through the Canadian Red Cross, the Government provided CAD200,000 to ICRC operations in Bosnia &amp; Herzegovina, and CAD200,000 to support ICRC efforts in Serbia. The Government of Canada also channelled CAD400,000 through Save the Children Canada to support work in Bosnia &amp; Herzegovina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The Royal Bank of Canada donated CAD50,000 to be used as most needed in Bosnia &amp; Herzegovina, Croatia, and Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> — Croatia provided two military transport helicopters to Bosnia and Herzegovina, one helicopter operating in the <a href="/wiki/Banja_Luka" title="Banja Luka">Banja Luka</a> – Doboj region, and one in Maglaj – Zenica region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> 6 teams of the <a href="/wiki/Croatian_Mountain_Rescue_Service" title="Croatian Mountain Rescue Service">Croatian Mountain Rescue Service</a> with 15 rescuers, and 25 members of the civil protection units and fire brigades with 10 vehicles and 3 boats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> 8 intervention policemen with boats are active in <a href="/wiki/Od%C5%BEak" title="Odžak">Odžak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ora%C5%A1je" title="Orašje">Orašje</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mup_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-mup-70">[70]</a></sup> Croatia also sent 65 tons of drinking water to affected areas in Serbia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> along with firefighting and civil defence intervention units with 15 members, 5 vehicles and 2 boats,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> and 9 intervention policemen (including divers) operating in the area of Obrenovac.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mup_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-mup-70">[70]</a></sup> The Croatian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> opened a donations account for victims of the floods in Croatia, Bosnia and Herzegovina and Serbia. On May 20, the Croatian Red Cross announced that 4,815,681.17 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Croatian_Kuna" title="Croatian Kuna">kuna</a> (€632,186.57 ) had been donated for the victims of the floods in Croatia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> 543,789.71 kuna (€71,386.90) for the victims in Bosnia-Herzegovina and 435,480.82 kuna (€57,168.47) for the victims in Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Humanitarian trucks travelling toward the affected areas through Croatia motorways were excluded from paying a <a href="/wiki/Road_pricing" title="Road pricing">toll</a>.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> — Czech Republic sent a rescue team with water pumps, a boat and seven vehicles for different purposes to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanjug_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-tanjug-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="630" data-file-width="990" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Estonia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Estonia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Estonia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Estonia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Estonia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Estonia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a> — Estonia sent a rescue team and €87,000 to Bosnia and Herzegovina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Estonia also participated in a relief effort in Serbia, together with other EU countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="810" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/45px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> — Bulgaria, Germany, Slovenia, Austria, the Czech Republic, France, Croatia, Lithuania, Latvia, Luxembourg, the UK, Slovakia, Belgium and Estonia responded to the request filed by Serbia and Bosnia &amp; Herzegovina through the Emergency Response Coordination Centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> As of 19 May, more than 220 rescuers from various EU countries are at locations in Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> — French humanitarian organization NVO sent help to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> French Ambassador to Serbia, Mr. François-Xavier Deniau, stated that France sent half of their total yearly emergency funds to Serbia. Major French emergency forces team of 40 members arrived in Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> — Germany sent 15 rescuers with three pumps, five trucks and an aggregate to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanjug_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-tanjug-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> — Hungary sent five boats and a rescue helicopter to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanjug_57-4"><a href="#cite_note-tanjug-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Iceland.svg/21px-Flag_of_Iceland.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Iceland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Iceland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Iceland.svg/42px-Flag_of_Iceland.svg.png 2x" width="21"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> — Icelandic government is donating 3 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISK" title="ISK">ISK</a> (€19,500) to Bosnia and Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1350" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/35px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/45px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> — India donated 100,000 $ of humanitarian aid to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.D0.98.D0.BD.D0.B4.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B0_.D1.83.D0.BF.D1.83.D1.82.D0.B8.D0.BB.D0.B0_100.000_.D0.B4.D0.BE.D0.BB.D0.B0.D1.80.D0.B0_.D0.A1.D1.80.D0.B1.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B8_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-.D0.98.D0.BD.D0.B4.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B0_.D1.83.D0.BF.D1.83.D1.82.D0.B8.D0.BB.D0.B0_100.000_.D0.B4.D0.BE.D0.BB.D0.B0.D1.80.D0.B0_.D0.A1.D1.80.D0.B1.D0.B8.D1.98.D0.B8-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="660" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/21px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/32px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/41px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 2x" width="21"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> — Medicines, blankets, raincoats, rubber boats and food were provided in Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Flag_of_Ireland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ireland.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Flag_of_Ireland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ireland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Flag_of_Ireland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Ireland.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> — Ireland provided aid worth 50,000 Euros through the NGO World Vision. Ireland released relief supplies worth 220,000 Euros that were distributed via the World Food Programme. This included tents, blankets and water purification tablets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="630" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/23px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/35px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/46px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> — The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Crescent_Society_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" title="Red Crescent Society of the Islamic Republic of Iran">Red Crescent Society of the Islamic Republic of Iran</a> will be sending humanitarian aid to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/45px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> — Four rescue boats and €200,000 of humanitarian aid for the people in Serbia will be sent from Italy, Italian Ambassador to Serbia Giuseppe Manzo has said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> — The Japanese government sent Bosnia and Herzegovina ¥10,000,000 worth of resources, and Serbia resources for use worth $100,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/23px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/35px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/46px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> — Luxembourg sent a rescue team of 24 members to northern Bosnia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="840" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/21px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/32px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/42px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png 2x" width="21"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> — <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Security_Force" title="Kosovo Security Force">Kosovo Security Force</a> Minister <a href="/wiki/Agim_%C3%87eku" title="Agim Çeku">Agim Çeku</a> offered to help by sending rescue teams to Bosnia and Serbia, but this offer was refused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1400" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Flag_of_Macedonia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Macedonia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Flag_of_Macedonia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Macedonia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Flag_of_Macedonia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Macedonia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> — 75 rescue workers and large groups of volunteers (150 volunteers from the city of Kumanovo, and many others from other cities), 45 pumps, 9 boats and various other equipment were sent. The Macedonian Red Cross, universities and private businesses have organized special fundraising events to support the victims of the floods. A telephone service is available so that people may donate. Many spots in the city of Skopje collect various kinds of aid. As of May 19, the telephone service has collected 7.3 million <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_denar" title="Macedonian denar">MKD</a> (€120,000) in aid. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_Orthodox_Church" title="Macedonian Orthodox Church">Macedonian Orthodox Church</a> also sent 3 million MKD (€50,000) in financial aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> — The Malaysian Relief Agency (MRA) had channelled aid totalling <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_ringgit" title="Malaysian ringgit">MYR</a> 43,780 (€10,000) in the form of food packs and health kits to the province of <a href="/wiki/Od%C5%BEak" title="Odžak">Odžak</a> in Bosnia and Herzegovina, the MRA also has launched a public fund since 24 May to assist the flood victims in response to the appeal by the Bosnian government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Beside that, a Malaysian newspaper, <a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(Malaysia)" title="The Sun (Malaysia)">The Sun</a> public fund had raised a total of MYR 1,128,911 (€268,296.99) from the Malaysian public including a personal donation from the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Berjaya_Group" title="Berjaya Group">Berjaya Group</a> and the owner of <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City F.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Tan" title="Vincent Tan">Vincent Tan</a> with MYR 500,000 (€114,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="320" data-file-width="640" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/23px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/35px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/46px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> — 41 soldiers of the Montenegrin army with 7 military SUVs, 6 trucks and additional equipment were sent to Obrenovac. Divers and alpinists from Special counter-terrorist police unit have been sent to Obrenovac. Over 70 professional rescuers and firefighters were also sent to Serbia. More than 200 volunteers went to Serbia to provide help. More have asked to join, but it was not possible to organize transport. Unknown number of boats and pumps was also sent along with the military, police and rescue units. Montenegrin government offered to put two helicopters at the disposal of Serbia and Bosnia but they weren't called for. Several municipalities, as well as some companies, have donated money. In several cities there were organised donations of foods, rations and clothes. The Directorate for Emergency Situations of the Ministry for Interior Affairs sent four trucks with blankets, raincoats and sleeping bags to Serbia and two to Bosnia. Numerous private companies sent supplies in food and water. The Montenegrin Red Cross opened two bank accounts for help to flooded areas, and, together with all Montenegrin mobile operators, organised a special number where people can donate money by sending an SMS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> About €550,000 was raised with SMS and the bank accounts as of 30 June 2014. Montenegrin Red Cross also gathered 264 tons of water, 15 tons of juice, 12.5 tons of food and 4.5 tons of hygiene products in relief efforts for Serbia and Bosnia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Montenegro" title="Football Association of Montenegro">Football Association of Montenegro</a> donated €40,000. Montenegrin prime minister <a href="/wiki/Milo_%C4%90ukanovi%C4%87" title="Milo Đukanović">Milo Đukanović</a> sent condolences to his Serbian colleague Aleksandar Vučić about deaths that occurred. Đukanović also said that Montenegro will provide aid and all of its help resources to the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Serbia" title="Government of Serbia">Government of Serbia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> — Dutch Minister of Foreign Affairs <a href="/wiki/Frans_Timmermans" title="Frans Timmermans">Frans Timmermans</a> said on 20 May that The Netherlands will donate €500,000 to Bosnia and Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1280" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> — Poland sent a rescue team of 37 firefighters to Bosnia, with special pumps and 15 fire trucks. The Polish soldiers from EUFOR are providing assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1100" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/21px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/32px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/41px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png 2x" width="21"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> — Kingdom of Norway, among first, supported with around €3.000.000 most vulnerable victims, as Ambassador to Serbia, Mr. Nils Ragnar Kamsvåg said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-102">[102]</a></sup> Norway then donated $627.000 to the Serbian Government to be used for water purification and water tanks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-102">[102]</a></sup> The Norwegian Red Cross raising funds for Serbia and Bosnia-Herzegovina, collecting around €190.000 by May 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Norwegian Embassy in Belgrade decided to create a relief fund with €500.000 for support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Norway also participated through United Nations support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> — Also heavily confronted with floods, Romania will send help to neighboring Serbia. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Victor_Ponta" title="Victor Ponta">Victor Ponta</a> announced that the Romanian authorities will send a large water removal generator and perishable items such as food, water, blankets, clothes, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> — Russia sent four <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-76" title="Ilyushin Il-76">Ilyushin Il-76</a> aircraft carrying 76 rescue workers including 20 divers and 70 tons of humanitarian aid to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Specialists from the Russian-Serb humanitarian center in Serbia were also participating in work dealing with flood consequences by providing mobile power stations and motor pumps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Russian aid has saved thousands of lives with one operation seeing almost 400 people rescued including at least 79 children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> — <a class="external text" href="http://www.humencanonline.sk/sk/aktualne/spolocnost/slovensko-poslalo-humanitarnu-pomoc-balkanu/" rel="nofollow">Slovak government sent 6 tons of humanitarian aid to Serbia (78 000 €)</a> and also <a class="external text" href="http://www.teraz.sk/zahranicie/slovensko-pomoze-srbsku-postihnutemu/84960-clanok.html" rel="nofollow">humanitarian aid for Bijeljina city in Bosnia (50 000 €)</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.futbalovysvet.sk/clanok/1350/krasne-gesto-fanusikov-trnavskeho-spartaka" rel="nofollow">Also the fans of two biggest Slovak football teams sent a financial aid about 40 000 €.</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> — Hours after Bosnia and Herzegovina and Serbia requested help, Slovenia decided to send a special unit of civil protection, along with four vehicles, 20 experts and two special pumps to Serbia, and two units with motor boats, a 12-member unit of civil protection, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovenian_armed_forces" title="Slovenian armed forces">Slovenian military</a> <a href="/wiki/Bell_412" title="Bell 412">Bell 412</a> helicopter with its crew and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovenian_police" title="Slovenian police">police</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AB_212" title="AB 212">AB 212</a> helicopter with two crews to Bosnia and Herzegovina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The day after another 26 civil protection members departed for Serbia, with four motor boats and six rescue vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> In addition, a Slovenian military <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_AS532_Cougar" title="Eurocopter AS532 Cougar">Eurocopter AS532 Cougar</a> helicopter was dispatched to Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> During the afternoon of May 19 Slovenia sent 22 tons of humanitarian aid to Bosnia and Herzegovina, which was followed with another 10 tons sent in the evening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtv22ton_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-rtv22ton-114">[114]</a></sup> Slovenian food company Žito have contributed an additional 11 tons of food aid which was sent to Bosnia and Herzegovina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtv22ton_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-rtv22ton-114">[114]</a></sup> On 20 May a Slovenian military convoy, containing 30 soldiers and 13 military trucks, departed towards the affected areas with another batch of humanitarian aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtv22ton_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-rtv22ton-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-siol20052014_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-siol20052014-115">[115]</a></sup> The convoy was joined by six civilian trucks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-siol20052014_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-siol20052014-115">[115]</a></sup> On the same day the Slovenian Government sent another special pump to Serbia, dispatched to the site of the threatened <a href="/wiki/TPP_Nikola_Tesla" title="TPP Nikola Tesla">TPP Nikola Tesla</a> power plant near <a href="/wiki/Obrenovac" title="Obrenovac">Obrenovac</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-siol20052014_115-2"><a href="#cite_note-siol20052014-115">[115]</a></sup> A civil initiative led by former professional basketball player <a href="/wiki/Radoslav_Nesterovi%C4%87" title="Radoslav Nesterović">Radoslav Nesterović</a> has gathered and sent more than 400 tons of aid during the first ten days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-delo27052014_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-delo27052014-116">[116]</a></sup> With the help of donations the <a href="/wiki/Slovenian_Red_Cross" title="Slovenian Red Cross">Slovenian Red Cross</a> sent a total of 100,000 euros to Bosnia and Herzegovina and Serbia; 50,000 to the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross_Society_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Red Cross Society of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Red Cross Society of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and 50,000 to the Red Cross of Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcross100k_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-redcross100k-117">[117]</a></sup> The Slovenian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caritas_(charity)" title="Caritas (charity)">Caritas</a> have sent an additional 10,000 euros. The Slovenian Red Cross have also sent 650 tons of humanitarian aid during May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtv_120vojska_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-rtv_120vojska-118">[118]</a></sup> On 1 June the Slovenian Government sent a <a href="/wiki/Company_(military_unit)" title="Company (military unit)">company</a> of 120 soldiers to the affected areas in Bosnia and Herzegovina, equipped with a variety of combat and off-road vehicles, equipment for water and soil sampling, chemical and veterinary laboratories, a unit of medical care and the department for the destruction of unexploded ordnance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtv_120vojska_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-rtv_120vojska-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1600" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> — Sweden donated pumping equipment, bought from the distributor Meris. The equipment was sold at non-profit levels to the Swedish government, which provided the €20,000 funding of the donation. Meris also donated three pumps on their own initiative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1000" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/16px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/24px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 2x" width="16"/>  </span><a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> — <a href="/wiki/Migros" title="Migros">Migros</a>, Switzerland's largest retail company, donated 500,000 CHF through the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Red_Cross" title="Swiss Red Cross">Swiss Red Cross</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> — Turkish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a> called Bosniak President <a href="/wiki/Bakir_Izetbegovi%C4%87" title="Bakir Izetbegović">Bakir Izetbegović</a> and Serbian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Vu%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Vučić">Aleksandar Vučić</a> to offer his heartfelt condolences on flood disaster. Also, PM said that Turkey stands ready to provide any assistance to Bosnia &amp; Herzegovina and Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Turkish <a href="/wiki/Disaster_and_Emergency_Management_Presidency" title="Disaster and Emergency Management Presidency">Disaster and Emergency Management Presidency</a> (AFAD) has sent a 41-person rescue team with a <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_C-130_Hercules" title="Lockheed C-130 Hercules">C-130 cargo aircraft</a> for search-and-rescue operations as well as much-needed supplies and equipment such as 125,000 <a href="/wiki/Sandbag" title="Sandbag">sandbags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blanket" title="Blanket">blankets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Engine-generator" title="Engine-generator">generators</a> to the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> — providing humanitarian assistance in the form of medicines, medical supplies, as well as wheat flour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
