<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a> — Crown Prince of Abu Dhabi <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Mohammed bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Mohammed bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a> told President <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Tomislav Nikolić">Tomislav Nikolić</a> that the UAE would send $10 million in aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> — On 19 May the UK sent 33 Flood Rescue personnel with 4 motor boats to Bosnia to provide assistance on the ground. The UK sent three experts as part of the EU's civil protection assessment and coordination team to Serbia, including an expert from the UK Fire and Rescue Service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Volunteers from Flooding on the <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Levels" title="Somerset Levels">Levels</a> Action Group (FLAG) with recent expertise in assisting in the Somerset floods, including volunteers from <a href="/wiki/Khalsa_Aid" title="Khalsa Aid">Khalsa Aid</a>, are also helping out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> — American helicopters helped rescue people in both Bosnia and Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The US Department of Defense announced that it would be sending 26 tons of humanitarian aid to Bosnia and Herzegovina, consisting of water purification units, water cans and kitchen equipment; sand bags and shovels; sleeping bags, blankets, sleeping mats and cots; generators and fuel; and wet weather gear and clothing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The US embassies in Bosnia and Serbia have also established processes that will provide additional funds and resources such as food, cots, blankets, water and fuel cans, portable kitchen sets, space heaters, generators and water pumps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> — donated to Serbia equipment for mobile toilets and generators worth $583,000 which was completely funded by Norwegian government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_102-3"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Celebrity_response">Celebrity response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Celebrity response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Novak_Djokovic" title="Novak Djokovic">Novak Djokovic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nenad_Zimonji%C4%87" title="Nenad Zimonjić">Nenad Zimonjić</a> showed their support for flood victims and appealed via <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> for donations to help the flood victims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Djokovic also criticized the lack of media coverage internationally, calling the media "idle".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Following his win over <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Nadal" title="Rafael Nadal">Rafael Nadal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Open_(tennis)" title="Italian Open (tennis)">2014 Italian Open</a>, he donated all of the $500,000 in prize money that he had received to the victims of the flooding and collected another $100,000 through the Novak Djokovic Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Stankovi%C4%87" title="Dejan Stanković">Dejan Stanković</a> Foundation collected and donated over €315,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></li>
<li>Singers <a href="/wiki/Lepa_Brena" title="Lepa Brena">Lepa Brena</a> and Saša Popović, who jointly own <i>Grand Productions</i>, donated €20,000 personally as well as €250,000 via United Group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></li>
<li>Romanian businessman <a href="/wiki/Ion_%C8%9Airiac" title="Ion Țiriac">Ion Țiriac</a>, owner of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mutua_Madrile%C3%B1a_Madrid_Open" title="Mutua Madrileña Madrid Open">Mutua Madrileña Madrid Open</a> tennis Masters Tournament, and a former tennis and hockey player, donated $100,000 to flooding victims in Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nikola_Pekovi%C4%87" title="Nikola Peković">Nikola Peković</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Timberwolves" title="Minnesota Timberwolves">Minnesota Timberwolves</a> donated €50,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Urban Book Circle donated over $50,000 CAD worth of sleeping bags and 300 kilograms of baby food to the areas affected in Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Angelina_Jolie" title="Angelina Jolie">Angelina Jolie</a> donated $50,000 to the US Red Cross for Bosnia and Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goran_Bregovi%C4%87" title="Goran Bregović">Goran Bregović</a> donated €20,000 for the towns of <a href="/wiki/Maglaj" title="Maglaj">Maglaj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ub,_Serbia" title="Ub, Serbia">Ub</a> and called for particular consideration for the affected <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a> families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ceca_(singer)" title="Ceca (singer)">Ceca Ražnatović</a> donated €20,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ana_Ivanovic" title="Ana Ivanovic">Ana Ivanovic</a>, who is a <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> Goodwill Ambassador for Serbia, donated €8,700.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emir_Kusturica" title="Emir Kusturica">Emir Kusturica</a> donated his helicopters to be used for rescuing people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Billy_Idol" title="Billy Idol">Billy Idol</a> pledged to donate part of his earnings from his concert in Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adriana_Lima" title="Adriana Lima">Adriana Lima</a> called for aid to Serbia through the Novak Djokovic Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></li>
<li>Dutch TV chef <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_van_Veen" title="Rudolph van Veen">Rudolph van Veen</a> cooked for mothers with children on May 20 in one of the centers for evacuees in Belgrade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander,_Crown_Prince_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia">Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Katherine,_Crown_Princess_of_Yugoslavia" title="Katherine, Crown Princess of Yugoslavia">Katherine, Crown Princess of Yugoslavia</a> visited Obrenovac, <a href="/wiki/Topola" title="Topola">Topola</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Natalinac&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Natalinac (page does not exist)">Natalinac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blaznava" title="Blaznava">Blaznava</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0abac" title="Šabac">Šabac</a> and Krupanj (along with the collective centers in <a href="/wiki/Karaburma" title="Karaburma">Karaburma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sur%C4%8Din" title="Surčin">Surčin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krnja%C4%8Da" title="Krnjača">Krnjača</a>) and donated aid in value of over €30,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miralem_Pjani%C4%87" title="Miralem Pjanić">Miralem Pjanić</a> (Bosnian international footballer) bought an entire pharmacy worth of medication to assist flooding victims in Bosnia and Herzegovina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Officials say it may take 5 years for agriculture in the affected regions to recover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The managing director of the Kolubara coal field stated that it would take one year for the Tamnava pit to be dredged and dried, while the Veliki Crljeni pit would take around two months to be operational again. He has stated that the Tamnava pit is now an artificial lake. The Kolubara coal fields are open pits from which coal is supplied to the <a href="/wiki/TPP_Nikola_Tesla" title="TPP Nikola Tesla">TPP Nikola Tesla</a>. There are enough stockpiles of coal at hand to bridge the period until the coal pits are fully operational, but the delivery system needs repairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b92.net_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-b92.net-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Development_and_Humanitarian_Aid" title="European Commissioner for Development and Humanitarian Aid">European Commissioner for Development and Humanitarian Aid</a> <a href="/wiki/Kristalina_Georgieva" title="Kristalina Georgieva">Kristalina Georgieva</a> stated that Croatia and Serbia have the possibility to apply for aid from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Solidarity_Fund" title="European Union Solidarity Fund">European Union Solidarity Fund</a>, up to one billion euro in one year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> but this was later rescinded as a misstatement of the Commissioner. The EU Solidarity Fund in 2014 is 500 million euros, while individual countries can expect around 10 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> The aid can be transferred if the damage is assessed to be over 0.64% of the country's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a>. For Serbia, that would be around 175 million euros in damages. Bosnia, not being a candidate or member country of the EU, is not eligible for aid from this fund.</p>
<p>Serbia applied for the World Bank aid credit, amounting to a total of 227 million Euros.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2014_Southeast_Europe_floods&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
